() , ? asked the Prime Minister, Minister of Internal Administration, and Deputy Minister of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order : (a) Will he inform this House separately (i) the number of vehicles obtained for each of the Ministers of Nation Building and his personal staff; (ii) the basis on which these vehicles have been obtained; and (iii) out of them the number of vehicles obtained on hire or contract basis? ( ) , ? asked the Minister of Irrigation and Water Management and Minister of Ports and Aviation : (a) Will he inform this House (i) the amount of money invested in Mihin Air by the Government or Government institutions; and (ii) the names of the directors and the shareholders of Mihin Air; (b) Will he table (i) the corporate plan of Mihin Air; and (ii) the interim accounts from the inception and the balance sheet as at today? asked the Minister of Education : (a) Will he inform this House (i) the extent of land belonging to Sujatha Balika Vidyalaya at Kumbiyangoda in Matale; (ii) whether the land on which a new three - sto-reyed building for the aforesaid school is being constructed, belongs to that school; and (iii) if not, whether action will be taken to acquire that land? (b) Will he take necessary action regarding the offi-cers who granted approval to construct a gov-ernment building on a land which has not been acquired? (c) Will he inform this House (i) whether the access road to the agricultural land adjoining the school belongs to the school premises; (ii) if not, name of the institution to which it be-longs; and (iii) whether the principal has the authority to fix a gate closing the aforesaid road belonging to another institution? (d) Is he aware that the principal is acting in an arbi-trary manner disregarding the order of the Dis-trict Co-ordinating Committee?

( - ) (The Hon. Ranil Wickremasinghe - Leader of the Opposition) Hon. Speaker, there are two options available. One is to get a time from you for the concerned people to meet you and take this up. I will put in brief what the reasons are. The Chief Whip is also not here today. So we will ask for a time. One is, if you read Article 65 with Articles 41C (2) and 41C (3), this is not valid. Secondly, going on the earlier instance, since I was a Member of that Constitutional

Council, we decided that when the then Secretary-General, Mr. Dhammika Kitulgoda was appointed to the post of Secretary of the Constitutional Council, both posts should not be held together and that immediately there was a vacancy Mrs. Wijesekera should be appointed as the Secretary-General. The President sent a letter appointing her for 14 days and then she continued. In that instance, the Constitutional Council had agreed on the appointment of Mrs. Priyanee Wijesekara as the Secretary-General. The matter in dispute was the manner of appointment. We did not agree with President Kumaratunga sending a letter because we told her that it is not valid. Then, finally she corrected it. This is different because in this instance the Constitutional Council has not even recommended the name. ( ) (Mr. Speaker) . ( ) (The Hon. Ranil Wickremasinghe) I do not want to take all these up here because it would take half a day. So may be we will get a time and then let them come and meet with you and then we can have the Party Leaders Meeting after that.

20 Sikh Regiment . Sikh Regiment . . - [ ] . . . Please, do not disturb me. . . 25,000 . ( ) (The Hon. Gamini Lokuge) . ( ) (The Hon. Lakshman Kiriella) . ( ) (The Hon. Gamini Lokuge) ? ( ) (The Hon. Lakshman Kiriella) 10,000 . , . 12 . . [ ] , . . ( ) (The Hon. Gamini Lokuge) , - [ ]

[ .] [ ] [Expunged on the order of the Chair.] , . Regiment . Sikh Regiment . . . 1948 , .

, , . 24 . 50 60 . . , . . . , . , . , . , . . . . ? . . . . . . , , . , ... , .. . . . , , . . ? . . . . . , . 51 . , . . . .

[.. 1.21] ... ( ... ) (The Hon. A.M.M. Nawshad)

Bismillahir Rahmanir Raheem.

Hon. Deputy Speaker, I am honoured that you are presiding even on the second occasion I got up to speak. When we debate the extension of the Emergency, I am reminded of an incident. I stated in my last speech here that the Government still fails to realize the mood of the

2008 06 133 134

people of the Eastern Province. When the Hon. (Ven.) Ellawala Medhananda Thero spoke before me, he quoted speeches made by the Leader of the Sri Lanka Muslim Congress and implied that they were basically communal. What I would like to remind this House is that this interpretation of the aspirations of different communities is something that has driven us to this situation today. I will quote a personal incident. In 1972, I applied to be an officer cadet of the Sri Lanka Army. I, being a Thomian and a coloursman in so many sports, was among the last 40 of which 25 were to be chosen. When I entered the interview room for the last interview, the question I was asked by an elite panel - I do not want to name them because some of them are no more with us - was, What is your name? I said, Nawshad. Then they asked me, What is your fathers name? I said, Abdul Majeed. The next question was, "Which Majeed, Nintavur Majeed or Pottuvil Majeed? At that time, my father was not alive, but he represented Nintavur and my present father-in-law, who was my maternal uncle at that time was the UNP Member of Parliament for Pottuvil. Then they asked me, "How is Pottuvil Majeed related to you?" I said, "He is my maternal uncle". Then I was asked to go. I was told, Okay, thank you. We will let you know. And when we inquired through the then Defence Minister, the Hon. Lakshman Jayakody, we were told, If you speak to Madam, he will be taken, because otherwise he has qualified." Incidents of this nature and seclusion of the minorities from the armed forces and the Government Service are what has driven the leaders of Muslim parties to ask for the just rights of their people. When you talk of betraying the country and communalism, what you should understand is that those are direct resultants of suppression of the just rights of the minorities. If I was chosen that day to serve this country, I would have been either dead or a brigadier; you would have had a Muslim in the hierarchy of the army. I had all the qualifications, but I was deprived of that opportunity because I was so-and-sos nephew. These are the incidents that have created this situation today. When venerable monks of the Buddhist faith keep on repeating this, I am reminded of an incident relating to haiku. I am not sure how many have heard of the Japanese form of poetry called haiku. There was a famous poet called Basho and he was walking with his disciple Hikaiku. Hikaiku saw a dragonfly and said, If you remove the pair of wings from a dragonfly, you will see a pepper pod." And Basho said, "That is not haiku. You should give life to something. That is haiku." Then he said, Why do you not say, "Give a pair of wings to a pepper pod, and you will have a dragonfly?" That is how the people of this country should think, especially those who sit in this House; that you should give life to something that is already dead. The relationship between the communities in this country is dead for no fault of the minorities but for the lack of

accommodation of their aspirations on the part of the majority. So, if the majority is not willing to look at giving life to something that is dead, we cannot dream of peace in this country. Then, speaking on the extension of the Emergency, I will speak more of its abuse. I just returned from my village, Samanthurai, where we had a mammoth election rally yesterday with the Leader of the Opposition presiding. We find the election atmosphere reflected in the House today because most of the Government benches are empty. All of them are very tired because they had been parading the East in convoys of 20 to 30 vehicles coming behind filled with people from outside the district, who basically fill up the empty seats at their meetings. But what is important here is the total abuse of State resources. All the candidates are provided with government vehicles. All the Ministers come in convoys of over 10 to 12 vehicles and one Ministers convoy, I personally saw yesterday, had four identical vehicles without number plates. This will not bring you votes. This will only keep on driving people away from you. There was a school-opening ceremony. Actually it was not an opening of a school; it was a building that was opened. I do not want to go into the history of the building, but what disturbed me most was this. I am the Member of Parliament of the area; but I was not invited. But I made it a point to be there on time because I knew there was a function. I went there at 9 oclock. The Hon. Minister came; I received him and told him, "Look, as the Representative of the people, I need to receive you and then you can go ahead with what you want to do. But what happened inside was that the teachers belonging to 64 schools signed officially and gathered at the National School. For the first time, I saw a cut-out of a politician hanging inside the school and what took place there was pure political talk. This is a violation of all election laws. You cannot use your ministerial powers to force Government servants to vote in favour of the Government. If you continue to do this, you will see a repeat of what took place in the North taking place in the East. I mentioned this in my last speech as well. If the State continues to suppress the rights of the minorities, the minorities will have no choice but to choose the path which they think will serve their purpose. The East is filled with checkpoints. I mentioned this in my last speech too. If any Member of this House can get into a bus from Kandy, Polonnaruwa or Hambantota and travel to the East, if he would do that for one day, I am sure he will come here, stand on his head and make sure that these checkpoints are removed. People are harassed. Even at 12 noon in the hot sun they have to get down, carry their bags and walk 100 to 200 metres to get into the bus again. Why? If the East is liberated, why should the people be harassed? All you have to do is to secure the borders and let the people defend themselves. When I travel from Samanthurai to Habarana, I have to go through around 15 checkpoints. Of course, as a Member of

135 136

Parliament I have the privilege of flashing this card and passing through. But what is the message I give to the people who stand there? I have no way of making life easy for them as it is for me. So, actually I am abusing my power as a Member of Parliament without allowing to be checked at these security checkpoints. I am sure when the Hon. Ministers went round touring the Eastern Province in their convoys, they would not even had to brake at those barriers because at all those checkpoints the lead vehicles would have been flashing the lights and they would have just breezed through. But this is what is pushing the minorities to look at other options. I am not blaming one Government; every Government does this. That is why the minorities continue to look at different options. I am urging the Government, please demilitarize the East. The Pilliyan group or the armed group that is operating in the East needs to be protected and security can be provided by the security forces, but they should not be allowed to go among the people with arms. And if this is not done, I am sure, the democratic will of the people will not prevail and you will find the rights of the minorities once again suppressed. Thank you.

[.. 3.35]

( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) , 40 .

( ) (The Presiding Member) . ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) 4.30 . Hon. Presiding Member, I thank you very much for giving me this opportunity to speak in this empty House. ( ) ( - ) (The Hon. Keheliya Rambukwella - Minister of Foreign Employment Promotion and Welfare) . . ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) . [Interruption.] When I said, "empty House", it is an empty House. ( ) (The Hon. Keheliya Rambukwella) You are right - [Interruption.] ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) That is right. I did not say it is on the Government side. I know your mind is in the East even though your body is here. ( ) (The Hon. Keheliya Rambukwella) In your case, your mind and body, both are there. ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) Anyway, this is a very critical moment. The country is going through a turbulent period. Our Hon. Minister of "Disinformation" is here; he is doing a yeoman service

165 166

with a bad brief. But, unfortunately, we are saddled with a situation where the country has plunged into deep darkness. Amidst this, today we are having an election in the Eastern Province. Now, this is not something what the people asked for. This is something which the Government has given in order to determine their political future. But, today it has become a centre of attraction where the entire Government is forced into a checkmate at the moment. Sir, all I could basically say is, since 1948 this country, a wonderful, beautiful and one of the nicest countries in the world, has been having its own share of problems. We, Sri Lankan citizens, have got to change the system and take it to a better tomorrow. But, it seems that always we do too little, too late. It has been the practice that when one party does something, the others oppose and vice versa. Today, I am happy to state that two major parties are at the helm of politics. All these fragmented political parties, to me, should be blown out of the political system democratically and that is where I think the two major parties, accepted or otherwise by the people, should be able to determine the future of this country. But, unfortunately, owing to petty politics, instead of targeting the country, they target individuals and we cannot see the wood for the trees. This is the time that we need to work together. I say this as I see how desperate the Government is and how the people are looking helplessly as to what could be done in order to protect themselves. It is no mean fun to see numerous debacles taking place. All of us, at the end of the day, see Sri Lankans losing. But, if this is something which is within our control and that is by choice and not by chance and if that is what leads to this problem, then, you have got to turn the searchlights in and ensure that we provide a solution to that. Now, that does not mean that since 1948 no government has been doing anything. All governments have been doing too little too late. Before we gained Independence, there was an attempt to find a solution. Then we gained Independence. After that, we had the Bandaranaike-Chelvanayakam Pact and the Dudley-Chelvanayakam Pact. Physically we managed to get a political process in place, the District Development Council. It had an impact on the Constitution and this moved forward. Unfortunately, it did not bring a solution. Then, with the passage of time, we saw the Thirteenth Amendment coming in and that went through one of the turbulent periods in this country where the principal Opposition then decided to take the Government head on. We had the blessings of India. Unfortunately, owing to the politicization, it was looked at with a warped eye and today we seem to be paying the price for that. The Government, after the Thirteenth Amendment was brought into the Constitution, and basically had an element of devolution of power. Many minority politicians said that was too centred. Just because we are the majority community, it does not mean that we are going to trample the minority communities. After all, the social fabric of this country is the getting together of the

Sinhalese, the Tamils, the Muslims, the Burghers and the Malays and that is why we are called "proud Sri Lankans". Unfortunately, we have never been able to put that social fabric together and the strength in diversity has never been used or put to test. We have been fighting one another but not able to put that strength together. After all, if we can put together the business acumen of the Muslims, the industriousness of the Tamils, the large heartedness of the Sinhalese, do you not think that we can get a very strong, healthy, Sri Lankan identity? Now, that is something which is eluding us and we need to come together in this hour of need. After the Thirteenth Amendment was brought in, there was an attempt to legislate certain things. There was once again, a political element. It was the former President Chandrika Kumaratunga who brought at that time, the 2000 Proposals. Unfortunately, once again it was viewed as trying to stay in power rather than bringing a solution to a vexed ethnic issue and owing to disagreement on certain minor points, we were unable to move forward. Then we saw the courageous and sagacious move of the Hon. Ranil Wickremasinghe signing the Ceasefire Agreement. That was something which was done with the country at heart. We inherited the country in a situation where bombs were going off in all areas and the economy was at its lowest ebb. In that situation, a Ceasefire Agreement was thought the best. It was signed. It moved forward. The test of time showed that we were able to contain the people who thought that fighting is better than talking. Finally, the people in the warring field decided to come to the negotiating table. They came; they spoke; they had differences. It was not a final cast-iron approach that was produced. It was a step-by-step going forward approach. Unfortunately, time and again it was politicized. We signed it on the 22nd of February, 2002 and we thought that was the dawn of a new future. Owing to the fact that it had the stupendous support even from the warring faction, it went forward. But, due to too much of optimism, there was a breakdown once again. There was an opportunity to get it move again. Unfortunately, politics played the devils advocate and Parliament was dissolved. Thereafter, we saw the present President Mahinda Rajapaksas Government coming in. They decided that the Ceasefire Agreement after five years, was not good enough. That is their choice and finally, today you would see that we have gone into the fourth battle. Today, we speak of the numbers that are killed. At this particular moment you could see that the United National Party has never dabbled in the number of people who are being killed, injured or anything like that but only dare to tell that, This is your choice. This is not something that was pushed upon you. This is something invited by yourself . Because of that fact we need to tell that those people laid down their lives just to gain political mileage. You cannot hide these facts. You need to take the

[ ]

167 168

2008 06

responsibility for that. If I may just go down memory lane, I recall the Hon. Prime Minister, from 9th January 2007, religiously telling us the figures as to how many personnel of the armed forces have been killed, how many have been injured and so on. I just tabulated these statistics so that we can compare the deaths that took place then and today. I am only comparing the deaths that took place from January 2007 to April 2008. We have got officially, as per the Hon. Prime Ministers statements, 824 deaths and 5,248 injured. As regards civilians, it is 926 deaths and 1,077 injured. So, what happened to the Government which came to power saying that within three months they would bring honourable peace? Effort to bring honourable peace was put aside by saying "Let us capture Mavilaru and thereafter we will ensure that peace dawns in this country". We looked at the things that were happening. It did not work the way they wanted. Then, there was an overture made to the United National Party, which resulted in the signing of an MoU. The MoU was signed. The MoU was thought to be the stepping stone or the starting point to the dawning of a new era. Months went by and then suddenly you saw the very hand that we extended to assist was chopped off. You proceeded from there. You said "Okay, let us put aside the MoU. Let us capture Thoppigala, let us capture Sampur". Day by day, new stories went around and you moved forward from Sampur to Thoppigala. "All captured", but only headlines and deadlines. Then you said "We need to pass the Budget in 2007. Therefore, everybody must rally around us and anybody who votes against the Budget is a traitor". Finally that was the slogan used to pass the Budget in 2007. They further said, "You would see a huge investment flowing into the country after the Budget is passed". But after passing the Budget that dream was also set aside. Then, you suddenly have some army officers appearing and setting 31st of March 2008 as the finale of this war. We kept on listening to them because we, as a responsible Opposition and a party that brought Independence to this country - our former leader, Right Hon. D. S. Senanayake with the help of everybody managed to get Independence to this country - have a right more than anybody else to ensure the protection of Mother Lanka. That is what we are talking about today. So, 31st March comes and goes. But nothing happens. Then deadlines change again. How long can you go on like this? That is why we are saying today that we must be truthful to the people of this country. There is a limit to lying. You can fool some people some time, some people all the time but not all the people all the time. That is what this Government seems to be doing. Therefore, we need to make the wake-up call. Today we had the Prime Minister stating the number of soldiers killed after the debacle of Muhamalai in April. I would like to quote the Secretary to the Ministry of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order, Mr. Gotabhaya Rajapaksa. I do not want to quote him to take any undue advantage. All I want to say is, if he as the Secretary to

the Ministry of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order spearheading this military effort, says that it was a debacle, we have got to see as to why he had said so. The Hon. Prime Minister informed this House that 120 soldiers, 56 civilians, 1,235 LTTEers had been killed and almost 945 soldiers had been injured. What a colossal loss of lives ! ( ) (The Presiding Member) Order, please! . , . , , . Whereupon THE HON. PIYANKARA JAYARATNE left the Chair, and MR. DEPUTY SPEAKER took the Chair. ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) Thank you. Mr. Deputy Speaker. I was just speaking about the present situation the Hon. Prime Minister informed this House. All I could basically say is that, we have already seen these young soldiers laying their lives for a better tomorrow for Sri Lanka. But all of them are helplessly looking forward to a future that is dark for them. They say that they fought on behalf of the country. But when you really go into the nitty-gritty of the situation to see as to why they had to sacrifice their limbs, eyes and ears, you will find that there is a political element in it. Has this not got to be questioned? Should we be silent on this? How many more have to pay the price before this nonsense is stopped? We have given unstinted support to you. We have never questioned your military aspects. We have given that right to His Excellency the President as well as to the Government. But after 31st of March it is incumbent on us also to tell that we are fighting on behalf of the people. We have the right to know. You are telling us something today and you are changing it tomorrow. You are trying to play politics all the time to show how weak the UNP is. What has happened today? It is retribution for what you have done. You used political parties. Today they are fragmented; they are disappearing. The people who used to character assassinate us are crying in this House saying what has happened to them. They say how difficult it is when it comes from their own house. All we want to say is that we went through it without a murmur. When they go through that after doing the same to others, we call it "retribution". But all we have got to say is, while these petty politics are going on, we, the two big parties, do not need to mess around with the country. We have been telling this right along. We have got to ensure that there is a political settlement. A military solution is what has been pursued. We gave you time. But at the

169 170

end of the day, you have got to ensure that this would come to a conclusion. There has to be culmination. The people of this country, at the end of the day, should not turn around and say, "The Members of the Thirteenth Parliament have been looking at their own interests, not at our interests". So, this is where we have got to change. Look at the solutions. My good Friend, the Hon. Senathirajah, the General Secretary of the ITAK, and we have been speaking on many matters. The Hon. Douglas Devananda may have a different opinion, but at the end of the day, we all climb the same hill from different approaches. We want to know what is going to be the solution. You have got maniacs, there are chauvinists; some have used religious parties and come in and they ruin the religion. We do not talk of those. Where are the two major parties? With the majority of the representatives of the Tamil people, let us come to a solution. - [Interruption.] There is only talk from that side. When they come on bended knees, you say, "Very good". Listen to what we have been telling from the day we came to Parliament. We were talking of the 50:50 solution. Then, you promised to bring in the "Sinhala Only" policy within 24 hours. Thereafter, there was standardization of education. I am speaking to my Tamil and Muslim Friends. I am mentioning here their grievances. There was standardization of education, the 1958 "Sri" riots, the 1983 riots, the Vadamarachchi IPKF operation, the Thirteenth Amendment, the capture of Jaffna by former President Chandrika Bandaranaike Kumaratunga, the Ceasefire Agreement and thereafter, President Mahinda Rajapaksa's military pursuit. All these, the Governments at that time decided, were the best for them. There is no question. I am sure no Government would do something which would jeopardize them or be injurious to themselves. But, at the end of the day when you look back, you must see how much it has moved the country forward or how much it has taken the country backwards. If we look at that, I am sure all of us will have tears in our eyes and this should not be at the expense of the country. I table*, Hon. Deputy Speaker, a document which is about 20 to 25 pages.

All I have done is, totalled the figures that appeared in all the military reports in the "Daily News", the "Lankadeepa", the "Dinamina" and in certain other newspapers. If you add the numbers of the terrorists who have been killed according to the Government newspapers, you will find that they have killed more than 10,000 LTTEers. If you look at reports in private newspapers, you will find that 6,000 Tigers have been killed. I am tabling that to go into Hansard and some day, some people will look back and find out who was conning whom.

Sir, I would also like to take up the cost that has been incurred through a series of Governments on the area of defence. In 1998, we have spent Rs. 44 billion; in 1999, Rs. 47 billion; in 2000, Rs. 83 billion; in 2001, Rs. 68 billion; in 2002, Rs. 63.26 billion; in 2003, Rs. 63 billion; in 2004, Rs. 75.87 billion; in 2005, it had been Rs. 86 billion. In 2006, we had spent Rs. 111 billion. In 2007, it had been Rs.140 billion and for the year 2008, we have allocated Rs. 167 billion with a further Supplementary Estimate coming in. If I just take the last three years, we have spent close to Rs. 500 billion, which is about US Dollars five billion, on just one aspect: on arming ourselves to fight the terrorists. It does not matter even if we spend US Dollars 10 billion if there is a collateral benefit to this. But have we gone forward? You say on one side, that you have moved forward and then the Secretary to the Ministry of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order comes and says there was a debacle in Muhamalai. When my good learned Friend, the Hon. Lakshman Kiriella, goes before the media and gives a genuine answer to the questions asked, his character is assassinated. Three weeks later, the very thing he had the courage to say was accepted by the Secretary to the Ministry of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order saying, yes. Why? Is there a battle between the forces, the commanders and the Secretary? Suddenly, the things that are kept back are brought out into the open. I do not want to go into that area because I think you can debate the motive of all these for days. But we have got to look at what is going on. Now, I would like to take up the present day situation. The Minister of Disinformation, the Hon. Keheliya Rambukwella is not there, but he has been repeatedly giving deadlines. He has been saying, No LTTE by the end of 2006, No LTTE by the end of 2007, No LTTE by 31st March, 2008 and I have got The Sunday Times of 27th April, 2008, which says, No LTTE by the end of the year: Govt.. So, we do not care tuppence for his deadlines. But, all we want to say is that you are flying the flag for the Government and the Government means we all put together. We may be in the Opposition today and in Government tomorrow. But at the end of the day, all the ill wills of the governments have to be shouldered by the successive governments. Today, see what is going on. Look at the impact on the Eastern Provincial Council Elections. Presently, the entire Government is focused on the eastern area. Today the people in Ampara, Trincomalee and Batticaloa are seeing Ministers they have never seen for the last, maybe, 60 years. They only see them during election time and they come back again only if there is another election. I have been in Trincomalee, Mutur, Kinniya, Kantalai, Seruwila, Tambuttegama and all those areas. , . - [ ]

* . . Document not tendered.

asked the Minister of Public Administration and Home Affairs (a) Will he inform this House of (i) the number of officials in each grade of the Sri Lanka Administrative Service; (ii) the positions and responsibilities held by the said officials separately on the basis of Ministries, Departments, Provincial Councils and other institutions;

(iii) the names of the officials who have retired from public service and are serving in the aforesaid institutions again; and (iv) the positions and responsibilities held by them, their ages and the class of the Sri Lanka Administrative Service to which they belonged at retirement? (b) Will he inform this House (i) on the basis of relevant institution, the number of Class I and Super Grade posts of the Sri Lanka Administrative Service approved by the Department of Management Services and exist in Ministries, Departments, Local Government institutions and various institutions; and (ii) the names of the persons who are acting in each of the aforesaid positions on retired and contract basis? (c) Will he state (i) the names of the persons who do not belong to the Sri Lanka Administrative Service and hold posts that belong to the Sri Lanka Administrative Service and approved by the Department of Management Services and the relevant positions held by them; and (ii) separately, the educational and professional qualifications of the aforesaid persons? (d) If not, why?

() ? asked the Prime Minister, Minister of Internal Admini-stration, and Deputy Minister of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order : (a) Will he inform this House (i) the number of Samurdhi recipients as at 30th June of every year from 2004 to 2007 in the Colombo-East electorate in Colombo District; and (ii) the categories of the above families accord-ing to the amount they received?

(b) Will he state (i) the value of inflation for the years 2004, 2005, 2006 and 2007; (ii) the value in real terms they received in the subsequent years up to 2007 when dis-counting the inflation taking 2004 as a base year; (iii) whether it shows that the purchasing power of the Samurdhi recipients has been re-duced; and (iv) as a result whether poverty has been in-creased among such recipients? (c) If not, why?

asked the Prime Minister, Minister of Internal Admini-stration, and Deputy Minister of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order, : (a) Will he inform this House (i) the number of Samurdhi recipients as at 30th June of every year from 2004 to 2007 in the Borella electorate in Colombo District; and (ii) the categories of the above families according to the amount they received? (b) Will he state (i) the value of inflation for the years 2004, 2005, 2006 and 2007 (ii) the value in real terms they received in the sub-sequent years upto 2007 when discounting the inflation taking 2004 as a base year; (iii) whether it shows that the purchasing power of the Samurdhi recipients has been reduced; and (iv) as a result whether poverty has been increased among such recipients? (c) If not, why?

() , ? asked the Prime Minister, Minister of Internal Admini-stration, and Deputy Minister of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order, : (a) Will he inform this House (i) the number of families received the Samurdhi subsistence dole from the Government as at 30th June of every year from 2004 to 2007 in the Puttalam District; and

(ii) the categories of the above families according to the amount they received? (b) Will he state

(i) the value of inflation for the years 2004, 2005, 2006 and 2007

(ii) the value in real terms they received in the sub-sequent years upto 2007 when discounting the inflation taking 2004 as a base year;

(iii) whether there is a drastic drop in the purchas-ing power of the Samurdhi recipients owing to the mishandling of the economy resulting a high inflation?

(c) If not, why?

Subscription : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available for Rs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to the SUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATION BUREAU, No. 132, Maya Avenue, Kirulapone, Colombo 5. The fee should reach him on or before November 30 each year . Late application for subscriptions will not be accepted.
